#### Instructions:

The shaded boxes within the checklist indicate an item is not required at a particular stage of review. Split cells vary by application type, per the key at the bottom of each page. Complete the unshaded boxes on the left side of the table for your applicable review stage(s) with an affirmation (Y, X, or ✔) or an indication that the requirement is not applicable to your application (N/A). If you cannot meet a checklist requirement, you must apply for and receive a waiver prior to the application being considered complete pursuant to § 200-38 of the Barrington Code of Ordinances. Please complete a separate copy of this document for each review stage. One copy may be submitted for combined review stages. Application materials shall be submitted in electronic .pdf format and shall legibly print at tabloid (11"x17") size unless otherwise indicated. Each page of submitted material shall have the date created and the name of the proposed development. Each stage of review shall include one full size paper copy to be kept by the Administrative Officer for public viewing. For the *Location*  column, provide the electronic file name and page number. This checklist pertains to the following development application review stages:

- 1. **A**dministrative **D**evelopment Plan Review (**AD**)
- 2. **M**aster Plan Review of a Major Land **D**evelopment Project (**MD**)
- 3. **P**reliminary Formal Development Plan Review or Preliminary Plan Review of a Major or Minor Land **D**evelopment Project (**PD**)
- 4. **F**inal Formal Development Plan Review or Final Plan Review of a Major or Minor Land **D**evelopment Project (**FD**)
- 5. **A**pproved Land Development Project or Approved Development Plan Review **P**lan (**AP**)

#### Town of Barrington Planning Board Regulations

Attachment 3: Development Review or Land Development Project Application Checklist

#### Drawing Submission Requirements:

- A. Master Plan Sketch.
  - 1. Name of proposed development, name of owner, name of the architect, engineers, landscape designer, and other consultants involved in the preparation of the plan, date, north point;
  - 2. Lots, including lot lines, approximate dimensions, approximate area and Assessor's lot numbers;
  - 3. Existing and proposed streets, approximate parking areas;
  - 4. Concept for collecting and discharging stormwater;
  - 5. Concept for grading, including limits of disturbance;
  - 6. Names of abutting property owners and property owners immediately across any streets adjacent to the subject parcel;
  - 7. Location and approximate size of existing buildings or significant aboveground structures on the subject parcel;
  - 8. Location of wetlands, watercourses or coastal features within and immediately adjacent to the subject parcel;
  - 9. Location of wooded areas and areas of agricultural use;
  - 10. Location of any unique or historic features, including historic cemeteries; within or immediately adjacent to the subject lot(s);
  - 11. Existing zoning on the site and on all abutting properties;
  - 12. Availability of utilities;
  - 13. Proposed buildings;
  - 14. Proposed number of building lots;
  - 15. Proposed number of dwellings;
  - 16. Concept for collecting and discharging stormwater; and
  - 17. Concept for grading, including limits of disturbance
- B. Site Plan. The applicant shall provide a proposed site plan for all areas of lots containing the entire tract, whether or not intended for development showing:
  - 1. Name of proposed development, name of owner, name of the architectural designer, engineers(s) (if applicable), landscape designer, and other consultants involved in the preparation of the plan, date, north point, scale, and legend;
  - 2. Name of proposed development, name of owner, name of the architect, engineers, landscape designer, and other consultants involved in the preparation of the plan, date, north point, scale, and legend;
  - 3. Lots, including lot lines, approximate dimensions, approximate area and Assessor's lot numbers;
  - 4. Existing and proposed streets, drives, parking areas (including arrangement and dimensions of parking spaces and drive aisles as well as points of ingress/egress), loading areas, and walks, including location, name and right-of-way widths on entire tract and on abutting property, as well as point(s) of access to the site;
  - 5. Utilities, indicating pipe sizes, grades, and manholes, proposed utility extensions, and text defining ownership and maintenance plans (water utilities to be verified by the Bristol County Water Authority and sewer utilities to be verified by the Department of Public Works);
  - 6. Topography, including contours at suitable intervals;
  - 7. Location of areas of active agricultural use or containing prime agricultural soils and farmland soils of statewide importance;
  - 8. Identification of the following areas of special concern:
    - a) Natural Heritage Areas, as defined by RIDEM
    - b) The area(s) under the jurisdiction of any Special Area Management Plan (SAMP) of RI CRMC
    - c) A Groundwater Protection Overlay District

#### Town of Barrington Planning Board Regulations

Attachment 3: Development Review or Land Development Project Application Checklist

- d) A Wellhead Protection Area
- e) Groundwater Recharge Area
- f) Areas within a TMDL watershed, as identified by RIDEM
- g) OWTS Critical Resource Area, as defined by RIDEM
- h) A Drinking Water Supply Watershed, as defined by RIDEM
- i) National Register of Historic Places
- 9. Coastal features, verified freshwater wetlands and the proposed drainage system;
- 10. Portions of the site located within a flood hazard area as identified by the Federal Emergency Management Agency's (FEMA's) "Flood Insurance Rate Map" and "Flood Boundary and Floodway Map" as may be amended;
- 11. Other conditions, including the location of rock outcrop, wooded areas, existing structures, embankments or retaining walls, railroads, power lines and significant physical features on the site and on adjacent land that may have an influence on the development of the site;
- 12. Public access areas, including parcels of land proposed to be dedicated for public use;
- 13. Solid waste collection areas;
- 14. Existing zoning on the site and on all abutting properties;
- 15. Location and orientation of all structures and their proposed uses identifying gross square footage of floor area according to § 185-8 of the Town of Barrington Code of Ordinances;
- 16. Proposed location and treatment of any public or private common areas or structures including open spaces, green roofs, plazas, parks or recreation areas. Applicant shall include a statement addressing long term maintenance of such areas;
- 17. Proposed renewable energy facilities and electric vehicle charging locations; and
- 18. The stamp of a RI licensed professional architect and engineer.
- C. Building Floor Plans and Structure Elevations. The applicant shall provide proposed structures elevations and floor plans for all buildings showing:
  - 1. Name of proposed development, name of owner, name of the architectural designer and other consultants involved in the preparation of the drawings, date, north point and scale;
  - 2. Name of proposed development, name of owner, name of the architect and other consultants involved in the preparation of the drawings, date, north point, scale, and legend;
  - 3. Base flood elevation data, if any portion of the proposed development is located within a flood hazard area as identified by the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA)'s "Flood Insurance Rate Map" and "Flood Boundary and Floodway Map" as being inundated during a one-hundred-year storm, as may be amended;
  - 4. General division of leasable units within structures and associated square footages, according to § 185- 8 of the Town of Barrington Code of Ordinances, including identification of affordable and market-rate housing units;
  - 5. Location of all building entrances and identification of which entrances shall be primary entrances, ADA accessible, exit only, and/or access-controlled;
  - 6. Areas of glazing and identification of operable windows; and
  - 7. Identification of façade materials.
- D. Landscape Plan. A landscape plan that indicates the general treatment proposed for the site, including the approximate amount, location and type of buffering, landscaping, hardscape and lighting proposed, as well as location and dimensions of pedestrian entrances, exits, and walkways. The landscape plan shall show existing trees greater than six inches (6") in diameter.
- E. Landscape Plan. A landscape plan, prepared by a landscape professional that indicates the general treatment proposed for the site, including the approximate amount, location and type of buffering,

The purpose of this letter is to certify items on the checklist item 5

This letter is certified as true and correct requesting the preliminary stage of approval and identifying any changes made to the application since the master stage of approval.

- 1. Coordination with fire department
- 2. Stormwater mitigation plan complete
- 3. Cart washdown area added to stormwater mitigation
- 4. CRMC assent filed for stormwater permit
- 5. Additional landscape elevations and rendering provided for cart barn
- 6. Proposed cart barn height reduced from 22' to 18.5'
- 7. Dumpster location added to plans
- 8. Coordination with utility departments

## "Southeast Corner"

Cart Barn + Multi Use Structure Preliminary Plan Narrative 03.04.25 Attn:

Town of Barrington RI Planning Board Site: AP 06-001, Nayatt Road. Barrington RI.

![](RICC Full Preliminary Package 3-4-25_attachments/_page_10_Picture_4.jpeg)

### Background on Rhode Island Country Club (RICC):

Located at 150 Nayatt Rd in Barrington, Rhode Island, exists the 1911 Donald Ross designed golf course known as Rhode Island Country Club (RICC). The course has a diverse mix of parkland, wooded and seaside holes, with the final four holes located on Narragansett Bay which offers views of the bay and its islands. This golf course is consistently ranked as one of top classic golf course in the country. It has hosted four USGA championships and is home of the CVS Charity Classic.

Throughout the years, renovations have been done to improve the golf course and associated facilities such as, a new dining room, members bar, camp room, fitness room and two golf simulators. RICC also offers other amenities such as tennis, squash, and paddle ball courts as well as a heated pool to enjoy with family and friends.

### Project Background:

The proposed project aims to facilitate the design of a new 1,170 sq ft ± multi-use building to accommodate the relocated paddle ball court, new tennis court, replacement of the existing cart barn with a new 6,417 sq ft ± cart barn in the south east corner of the property. The parking area will also be reconfigured by demolishing the existing amenities and will provide an opportunity for beautification of the surrounding area and provide space and access for the abovementioned facilities. The proposed facilities will increase parking requirements, these requirements are remedied by redesigning the existing parking lot immediately adjacent the projects area of concern and providing additional spaces that meet zoning requirements.

A pre-application town meeting was conducted by video call on October 24, 2024. The master planning board meeting was held on January 7, 2025 where master plan and special use was conditionally approved. The plans have been updated, based on the comments from the meeting, conditions of approval, a full stormwater design, as well as updated survey, soils and utility research. The property is zoned RE, which requires a special use permit for the current use of the "Golf Course." The prior special use permit was approved in 2015 to add a 116' x 43' building, move gasoline lines, add storage bins, complete paving, and add a loft to the existing building (BK 1430 PG 273).

### Existing Conditions

The existing lot is owned by the Rhode Island Country Club which provides their 138.2 acre lot to private members on Nayatt Road in Barrington. The lot itself exists just south of Echo Lake (RI0007020L-07) nestled between S Lake Drive to the north, Nayatt Road to the south, Washington Road to the west, Middle Highway to the east and resides just north of Upper Narragansett Bay (RI0007024E-01A). The coverage of the lot is

1

predominantly grasslands of low slopes with varying, sporadic vegetation. Unnamed water bodies (Golf Water Features) and Mussuchuck Creek (RI0007020R-01) run east to west through the mid portion of the property. Wetlands exist to the north of the project site (CRMC jurisdiction), near to CRMC jurisdictional areas. If required, an Assent will be applied for, when the projects' RIPDES permit is submitted. The projects area of concern is in the southeastern most area of the site, directly east of residential properties and north of Nayatt Road. The project area consists of the existing cart barn, paddle ball courts, tennis courts, parking area, tennis clubhouse, storage areas, and sheds. The main entrance for this project is east of the paddle ball courts. The existing lot has approximately 153,000 sq ft ± with various impervious covering about 2.5 % ± of the lot.

### Proposed Site Plan

The proposed improvement of this project is to install a 65'x18' multi-use building, 122'x50' cart barn, add an additional a tennis court, and relocate the paddle ball court. Existing facilities including the cart barn, warehouse, paddle ball court, and multiple utility sheds will be demolished to accommodate these site improvements. The proposed multi-use building shall be a 1-story building with a crawl space for storage capability. The proposed cart barn shall be 1 story building with slab on grade, placed in the same location as the existing cart barn. The purpose of the project is not to add new uses, per se, but to relocate the paddle ball courts, and increase the size of the cart barn. The project does propose to install an additional tennis court.

The proposed cart barn will not store any chemicals inside the facility. All chemicals are stored in the warehouse off Legion Way (see Figure 1). The golf carts are electric served with Lead-Acid Batteries.

![](RICC Full Preliminary Package 3-4-25_attachments/_page_11_Picture_4.jpeg)

Figure 1: Location of property chemical in relation to the project site (google.com)

The parking requirements are determined by gross floor area (GFA) with an approximate increase of 200 sq ft GFA. The current site configuration of the subject area and the parking area surrounding the club house provides a total of 158 parking spaces with 6 ADA spaces. The existing parking spaces surpasses the 130 spaces per GFA required. The parking table can be found within the civil plan set (C-200). The proposed conditions reconfigure the adjacent parking lot with landscape islands to accommodate 7 additional parking spaces, 2 of which to provide ADA access to the proposed multi-use building. A bike rack is also proposed near the ADA ramp to accommodate members who may travel to this area on a bicycle.

Parking is adequate for the proposed use, based existing and expected parking demand, it is neither insufficient nor will it result in unauthorized or excessive parking. The proposed parking also will not result in an excess of impervious surfaces for stormwater runoff.

The property has two existing entrances that will remain as is and traffic patterns around the existing parking lot will remain the same. The general entrance fronting the subject property will be remain intact continuing to serve the Club access to Nayatt Road.

### Proposed Utilities

A sewer connection ties into the existing warehouse building via Nayatt Road to the south from the north side of the building traversing the site via the east side of the building. A sewer connection will be required to connect the multi-use building and the updated cart barn and is proposed to tie into the existing service. A water connection serves the existing cart barn off Nayatt Road near the intersection with Middle Highway. A new water line is proposed to connect to the multi-use building and cart barn. The existing irrigation system will need to be relocated around the proposed structures. Coordination with BCWA will be completed to determine the size of the new line and possible lateral locations.

According to RI Energy, there is an existing 2" gas service in use for the existing paddleball courts and an there is an existing service for the cart barn. A new gas service will be installed for the multi-use building, the relocated paddleball court, and updated cart barn.

The existing warehouse and cart barn are served overhead by electricity from an on-site utility pole. Proposed conditions will relocate this utility pole and connect to the proposed facilities with a new transformer and underground electric service. NEI will continue to coordinate with RI Energy through design and construction to ensure the site infrastructure meets their requirements.

The existing parking lot lighting will remain and any additional lighting to the site will be building mounted and dark sky compliant.

After correspondence with DOT, a DOT utility permit will be required for the proposed water service connection. This permit will be filed for in the online DOT portal at a later stage. A DOT physical alteration permit is not required.

### Stormwater Requirements

The stormwater system for the project has been designed with the Redevelopment guidelines in the Rhode Island Stormwater Design and Installation Standards Manual. Overall, the project will result in a reduction in impervious area of approximately 333 SF.

The project will include three bioretention areas to treat and mitigate peak runoff rates and volumes. Curb cuts are installed in paved parking areas to convey stormwater runoff to best management practices (BMP's), which are designed to reduce the peak flow rate discharged from the site and provide total suspended solids (TSS) removal. Three bioretention areas have been designed with site grading to convey stormwater to the proper areas.

A cart washdown area is located off the southwest corner of the cart barn. The cart washdown process is comprised of a power washer hooked up to a hose spigot on the south side of the cart barn. No cleaners are used during the power washing. The golf carts are electric, so there is no concern about fuel, oil, or being a land use with higher potential pollutant loads (LUHPPL). The carts will be sprayed down over a crushed stone area that includes a subdrain, which will direct the runoff into the sediment forebay prior to discharging into the bioretention area. The discharge from this bioretention area is directed to a second bioretention system prior to being discharged to the final design point. The bioretention areas have been sized to accommodate this additional volume of runoff. In addition, it is not expected the cart wash area will be utilized during a rain event.

A CRMC Assent has been submitted and filed with CRMC for a stormwater review. As part of this CRMC submission, some revegetation of previously cleared areas is proposed.

### Potential Impacts

Being well within the scenic areas stated within the Barrington Comprehensive Plan, much care was taken to ensure that the proposed work falls within the scope of "betterment of the existing facilities to better serve the private residents of Barrington". Potential impacts are minimized with this redevelopment site work due to all work occurring within the limits of the site. The limit of disturbance has been minimized to either reduce or eliminate impacts to off-site features including neighboring residents and public right-of-way. The proposed work is within the zoning use of the property under recreation and the change in land use is negligible thus maintaining or elevating the value of the property and surrounding area.

#### Conclusion

All of the proposed improvements to the project's area of concern are necessary for the functional use of the country club, its amenities, and the needs of the club members. The existing cart barn, storage building, and surrounding area are obsolete and in need of improvement to be consistent with the condition country clubs' amenities.

The improvements to the project's area of concern include additional parking, additional landscaping area, and improved stormwater facilities where no stormwater facilities exist other than catch basin drywells. The proposed landscaping will also improve the appearance of the property along Nayatt Rd. The project improvement meets or exceeds all the requirements of the Town, the Rhode Island DEM Stormwater Manual, and CRMC.

 If you have any questions or concerns, please do not hesitate to contact Craig Barry (cbarry@neicds.com) from my office.

### EROSION AND SEDIMENT CONTROL NOTES:

- ALL EROSION CONTROL SHALL BE IN ACCORDANCE WITH RHODE ISLAND SOIL EROSION AND SEDIMENT CONTROL HANDBOOK,
- THE CONTRACTOR SHALL BE RESPONSIBLE FOR INSTALLATION AND MAINTENANCE OF ALL SEDIMENT AND EROSION CONTROL
- MEASURES SHOWN ON THESE PLANS. EROSION AND SEDIMENT CONTROL MEASURES SHALL BE INSPECTED AND MAINTAINED ONCE WEEKLY OR AFTER EVERY RAINFALL EVENT
- SEDIMENT BUILD UP GREATER THAN ONE-HALF THE BARRIER HEIGHT SHALL BE REMOVED AND DISPOSED OF PROPERLY AS REQUIRED. ANY SEDIMENT BUILD UP OUTSIDE OF THE SEDIMENT BARRIER SHALL BE REMOVED IMMEDIATELY
- CONTRACTOR SHALL MAINTAIN A RESERVE OF EROSION CONTROL MATERIALS FOR EMERGENCY USE AND ROUTINE MAINTENANCE. THE CONTROLS SHOWN ON THESE PLANS ARE INTENDED AS MINIMUM MEASURES. ADDITIONAL MEASURES MAY BE REQUIRED AND SHALL BE IMPLEMENTED BY THE CONTRACTOR IF WARRANTED OR REQUESTED BY THE OWNER, OWNERS REPRESENTATIVE,
- ENGINEER, OR ANY APPLICABLE REGULATING AGENCY. PRIOR TO THE START OF ANY LAND CLEARING / GRUBING OR OTHER CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITY THE PERIMETER CONTROLS SHALL BE PLACED, PROPERLY CONSTRUCTED AND CLEARLY VISIBLE. THESE CONTROLS SHALL REPRESENT THE LIMITS OF WORK AND WORKERS SHALL BE NOTIFIED THAT NO CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITY IS ALLOWED
- IF OR AS POSSIBLE CONSTRUCTION SHALL BE PHASED TO LIMIT TO THE MAXIMUM EXTENT PRACTICABLE THE AMOUNT OF EXPOSED SOILS. ALL DISTURBED AREAS SHALL BE TEMPORARILY OR PERMANENTLY STABILIZED WITHIN 14 DAYS OF COMPLETION OF GRADING ACTIVITIES.
- THE CONTRACTOR SHALL SCHEDULE WORK IN A WAY TO ALLOW POSITIVE DRAINAGE OF SUBGRADE THROUGHOUT CONSTRUCTION CONSTRUCTION ENTRANCES PER RIDOT STANDARD DETAIL 9.9.0 SHALL BE EMPLOYED AT ALL POINTS OF INGRESS AND EGRESS
- TEMPORARY DIVERSIONS, SEDIMENT BASINS, AND TEMPORARY SWALES MAY BE USED AND SHALL BE SIZED ACCORDING TO THE RHODE ISLAND SOIL EROSION AND SEDIMENT CONTROL
- CATCH BASINS AND STORM DRAINS SHALL BE PROTECTED PER RIDOT STANDARD DETAIL 9.8.0 IN GRASSED AREAS OR SEDIMENT BAGS IN
- TEMPORARY SEDIMENT STOCK PILES SHALL BE KEPT MOIST AND COVERED AT ALL TIMES. CALCIUM CHLORIDE SHALL ONLY BE USED IF AN APPROVAL FROM THE TOWN/CITY OR OTHER APPLICABLE AGENCY HAS BEEN GRANTED.
- DEWATERING FROM EXCAVATIONS WILL BE CONVEYED BY HOSE TO AN UPLAND AREAS AND DISCHARGED INTO A DEWATERING BASIN PER RIDOT STANDARD 9.7.0, HAYBALE CORRALS, OR SEDIMENTATION BAGS. THE CONTRACTOR SHALL ENSURE THAT NO CONTAMINATE IS PRESENT IN ANY WATERS PRIOR TO DISCHARGE FROM SITE AND IS RESPONSIBLE FOR ALL ENGINEERING, EQUIPMENT, MATERIAL AND LABOR REQUIRED FOR THE SITE WATER REMOVAL DURING CONSTRUCTION.
- CONSTRUCTION WASTE MATERIALS SHALL BE KEPT ON-SITE AND DISPOSED OF IN AN APPROVED AND APPROPRIATE MANNER IN ACCORDANCE WITH ALL APPLICABLE REGULATORY AGENCIES. RIPRAP SHALL BE USED WHERE NECESSARY TO CONTROL EXIT
- NON MOBILE (I.E. TRACKED MACHINERY) SHALL BE MAINTAINED WITHIN THE LIMIT OF DISTURBANCE DEFINED BY SEDIMENT
- . NEWLY VEGETATED AREAS SHALL BE REGULARLY INSPECTED AND MAINTAINED TO ENSURE ESTABLISHMENT OF APPROPRIATE
- THE CONTRACTOR SHALL NOT REMOVE ANY EROSION AND SEDIMENTATION CONTROL MEASURES UNTIL FINAL ACCEPTANCE
- OF THE SITE HAS OCCURRED. ALL DRAINAGE STRUCTURES SHALL BE CLEARED OF ACCUMULATED
- SEDIMENT PRIOR TO THE FINAL SITE ACCEPTANCE. TEMPORARY VEGETATIVE COVER SHALL BE APPLIED TO ANY DISTURBED AREAS (INCLUDING SOIL STOCKPILE AREAS) THAT HAVE NOT YET REACHED FINISH GRADE AS SOON AS POSSIBLE, BUT NOT MORE THAN 14 DAYS AFTER THE CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITY IN THA AREA HAS A TEMPORARY ASSIST UNLESS THE ACTIVITY IS TO RESUME WITHIN 21 DAYS. THE RECOMMENDED TEMPORARY SEATING DATES ARE MARCH 15 TO NOVEMBER 15 WITH THE APPROVAL OF THE ENGINEER.THIS TEMPORARY VEGETATIVE COVER SHALL CONSIST OF 60% OF ANNUAL OR PERENNIAL RYEGRASS AND 40% OF MULLET OR SUDAN GRASS OR 100% OF WINTER RYE. ANNUAL OR PERENNIAL RYEGRASS SHALL BE PLANTED AT THE RATE OF 1.5 POUNDS PER 1000 FT.2. WINTERIZE SHALL BE PLANTED AT A RATE OF 2.5 POUNDS PER 1000 FT.2, AND MILLET OR SUDAN GRASS SHALL BE PLANTED AT A RATE OF 1 POUND PER 1000 FT.<sup>2</sup>

LIMESTONE AND FERTILIZER SHALL BE APPLIED ACCORDING TO SOIL TEST RECOMMENDATIONS OFFERED BY THE UNIVERSITY OF RHODE SLAND SOIL TESTING LABORATORY. IF SOIL TESTING IS NOT FEASIBLE ON SMALL OR VARIABLE SITES, OR WHERE TIMING IS CRITICAL, FERTILIZER MAY BE APPLIED AT THE RATE OF 300 POUNDS PER ACRE OR 7 1/2 POUNDS PER 1000 FT.<sup>2</sup> OF 10 – 10–10 OR EQUIVALENT. APPLY LIMESTONE EQUIVALENT TO 50% CALCIUM PLUS MAGNESIUM OXIDE AS FOLLOWS: (1 3 TONS PER ACRE OR 135 POUNDS FOR 1000 FT.2 FOR CLAY, CLAY LOAM, AND HIGH ORGANIC SOIL (2) 2 TONS PER ACRE OR 90 POUNDS FOR 1000 FT.2 FOR SANDY LOAM, LOAM, SILTY LOAM, AND (3) 1 TON PER ACRE OR 45 POUNDS PER 1000 FT.2 LOAMY SAND OR SAND. TEMPORARY VEGETATIVE COVER SHALL BE INSTALLED AS OUTLINED IN THE RHODE ISLAND SOIL EROSION AND SEDIMENT CONTROL HANDBOOK.

2. PERMANENT VEGETATIVE COVER SHALL BE APPLIED TO ALL DISTURBED AREAS THAT HAVE REACHED FINISH GRADE AS SOON AS POSSIBLE, BUT NO MORE THAN 14 DAYS AFTER THE CONSTRUCTION ACTIVITY IN THAT AREA HAS PERMANENTLY CEASED. THE RECOMMENDED PERMANENT SEATING DATES ARE APRIL 1 TO MAY 31 AND AUGUST 15 TO OCTOBER 15. PERMANENT VEGETATIVE COVER OUTSIDE OF DETENTION BASINS, IMPERVIOUS SURFACES, OR NOT OTHERWISE SPECIFIED ON THE LANDSCAPE

APPLICATION RATE: 1.75 LBS/ 1,000

APPLICATION RATE: 0.35 LBS/ 1,000 15% OF KENTUCKY BLUEGRASS APPLICATION RATE: 0.11 LBS/ 1,000

5% OF PERENNIAL RYEGRASS APPLICATION RATE: 0.11 LBS/ 1,000

LIMESTONE AND FERTILIZER SHALL BE APPLIED ACCORDING TO SOIL TEST RECOMMENDATIONS OFFERED BY THE UNIVERSITY OF RHODE ISLAND SOIL TESTING LABORATORY. IF SOIL TESTING IS NOT FEASIBLE ON SMALL OR VARIABLE SITES, OR WHERE TIMING IS CRITICAL, FERTILIZER MAY BE APPLIED AT A RATE OF 500 POUNDS PER ACRE OR 11.5 POUNDS PER 1000 T.2 OF 10-20 DASH 20 OR EQUIVALENT. APPLY LIMESTONE EQUIVALENT TO 50% CALCIUM PLUS MAGNESIUM OXIDE AS FOLLOWS: 4 TONS PER ACRE OR 180 POUNDS PER 1000 FT.2 FOR CLAY, CLAY LOAM, AND HIGH ORGANIC SOIL: 3 TONS PER ACRE OR 135 POUNDS PER 1000 FT.2 FOR SANDY LOAM, LOAM, OR SILT LOAM: AND 2 TONS PER ACRE OR 90

THE USE OF HAY IS NOT ALLOWED. ALL REFERENCES TO HAY, SHALL BE

### **GRADING AND UTILITIES NOTES:**

- THE CONTRACTOR SHALL BE RESPONSIBLE FOR VERIFYING THAT THE PROPOSED WORK SHOWN ON THESE PLANS DO NOT CONFLICT WITH ANY EXISTING CONDITIONS OR OTHER PROPOSED WORK. IF CONFLICTS ARISE THE CONTRACTOR SHALL NOTIFY THE OWNER AND ENGINEER PRIOR TO INSTALLATION OF ANY PORTION OF THE SITE WORK WHICH WOULD BE AFFECTED. NO FIELD ADJUSTMENTS IN THE LOCATION OF SITE ELEMENT SHALL BE MADE WITHOUT THE ENGINEERS APPROVAL
- WHERE AN EXISTING UTILITY IS FOUND TO CONFLICT WITH WORK, THE LOCATION, ELEVATION, SIZE AND MATERIAL SHALL BE ACCURATELY DETERMINED BY THE CONTRACTOR IMMEDIATELY AND THE INFORMATION FURNISHED TO THE ENGINEER FOR RESOLUTION. THE CONTRACTOR SHALL NOT CONTINUE WORK ON AFFECTED UTILITIES UNTIL THE CONFLICT
- ALL WORK PERFORMED AND ALL MATERIALS FURNISHED SHALL CONFORM WITH THE LINE AND GRADES ON THE PLANS AND SITE WORK
- THE CONTRACTOR SHALL PROTECT ALL UNDERGROUND UTILITY FACILITIES FROM EXCESSIVE VEHICULAR LOADING. ANY DAMAGE RESULTING TO THESE FACILITIES SHALL BE RESTORED TO THEIR ORIGINAL CONDITION AT
- ALL WATER WORKS SHALL HAVE 5 FEET OF COVER
- GAS, ELECTRIC, AND COMMUNICATIONS ROUTING ARE SUBJECT TO REVIEW AND APPROVAL BY UTILITY COMPANY
- DURING CONSTRUCTION CONTRACTOR SHALL PROTECT EXITING UTILITIES BY PROVIDING TEMPORARY SUPPORTS OR SHEETING AS REQUIRED AT NOT ADDITIONAL COST TO THE OWNER
- EXCAVATION REQUIRED WITHIN THE PROXIMITY OF EXISTING UTILITY LINES SHALL BE DONE BY HAND. CONTRACTOR SHALL REPAIR ANY DAMAGE TO EXISTING UTILITY LINE OR STRUCTURES INCURRED DURING CONSTRUCTION N/F: Rhode Island Country Club OPERATION AT NO COST TO THE OWNER

## LOAM AND SEED:

ALL DISTURBED AREAS TO BE LOAMED AND SEEDED PER "RHODE ISLAND SOIL EROSION AND SEDIMENT CONTROL HANDBOOK" AS AMENDED OR REVISED FOR NON-NATIVE PLANTING SEEDING DATES ARE APRIL 1 THROUGH JUNE 15 AND AUGUST 15 THROUGH SEPTEMBER 30, DATE MAY BE EXTENDED 15 DAYS IN NEWPORT COUNTY

FOR NATIVE PLANING SEEDING DATES ARE BETWEEN AUGUST AND SEPTEMBER

LOOSEN SOIL TO A DEPTH OF FIVE INCHES BY RAKING, DISCING, DRAGGING OR TRAVERSING WITH TRACKED MACHINERY, OVER COMPACTION SHALL BE AVOIDED CLEAT MARKS SHALL BE PERPENDICULAR TO ANTICIPATED DIRECTION OF SURFACE WATER FLOW

APPLY TOPSOIL IF NECESSARY APPLY SLOW RELEASE FERTILIZER NOT TO EXCEED 1500 LBS PER ACRE OR 36 LBS PER 1,000 SF USING THE FOLLOWING PERCENTAGES BY WEIGHT

- 10% AVAILABLE NITROGEN (N)
- 20% AVAILABLE PHOSPHORIC ACID (P)
- 20% AVAII ABI F POTASSIUM (K)
- REMOVE FROM SURFACE ALL STONES LARGER THAN 2" IN DIAMETER, ALL DEBRIS, TREE ROOTS OR OTHER UNSUITABLE MATERIAL
- INSPECT AREA TO BE SEEDED IMMEDIATELY PRIOR TO SEEDING FOR ANY COMPACTED AREAS, IF COMPACTED AREAS EXIST SCARIFY PRIOR TO COMMENCING SEEDING

APPLY SELECTED SEED AT RATES PROVIDED UNIFORMLY MY HAND, CYCLONE SEEDER, DRILL, CULTIPACKER TYPE SEEDER OR HYDROSEEDER

- NORMAL SEEDING DEPTH IS .25 TO .5 INCH. HYDROSEEDINGS MAY BE LEFT ON THE SOIL SURFACE
- WHERE FEASIBLE, EXCEPT WHERE EITHER CULTIPACKER TYPE SEEDER OR HYDROSEEDER IS USED, FIRM THE SEEDBED FOLLOWING SEEDING OPERATION WITH ROLLER, OR LIGHT DRAG. SEEDING RATES SHALL BE INCREASED BY 10% WHEN USING HYDROSEEDING
- USE OF STRAW MULCH HELD WITH ADHESIVE MATERIALS OR 500 LBS PER ACRE OF WOOD FIBER MULCH IS RECOMMENDED FOR PROTECTION FROM SOIL EROSION. IF SEEDING CAN NOT BE COMPLETED WITHIN SEEDING DATES USE MULCHING TO PROTECT SITE AND DELAY SEEDING UNTIL THE NEXT RECOMMENDED SEEDING PERIOD.

WITH THE APPLICABLE PROVISIONS OF SECTION 212 OF RIDOT STANDARD SPECIFICATIONS FOR ROAD AND BRIDGE 1' MIN -

NYLOPLAST 24" DRAIN BASIN: 2824AG X

(5) ADAPTER

VARIABLE 0° - 360°

### RECOMMENDED SEEDING

### SPECIFICATIONS F.5.2.2 Bioretention Soil

The soil should be a uniform mix, free of stones, stumps, roots or other similar objects larger than two inches. No other materials or substances should be mixed or dumped within the bioretention area that may be harmful to plant growth, or prove a hindrance to the planting or maintenance operations. The bioretention soil should be free of noxious

The bioretention system shall utilize planting soil having a composition as follows:

Sand: 85-88%

Soil fines: 8 to 12% (no more than 2% clay)

Organic Matter\*: 3 to 5%

\*Note: For bioretention applications with a soil depth of less than 4 feet, add 20% (by volume) of well aged (3 months), well aerated, leaf compost (or approved

the above planting soil mixture. Where soil fines content is less than 12%, add a corresponding % of leaf compost.

A textural analysis is required to ensure the bioretention soil meets the specification listed above. The bioretention soil should also be tested for the following criteria: | pH range 5.2 - 7.0

magnesium not to exceed 32 ppm

phosphorus P2O5 not to exceed 69 ppm

potassium K2O not to exceed 78 ppm

soluble salts not to exceed 500 ppm All bioretention areas should have a minimum of one test. Each test should consist of both the standard soil test for pH, phosphorus, and potassium and additional tests of organic matter, and soluble salts.

Since different labs calibrate their testing equipment differently, all testing results should come from the same testing facility.

Should the pH fall out of the acceptable range, it may be modified (higher) with lime or (lower) with iron sulfate plus sulfur.

## F.5.2.3 Mulch Layer Specifications.

SLOPE VARIES MATCH FINISHED GRADE OR

AS SHOWN ON PLANS

PARKING LOT CROSS SECTION - FULL DEPTH

SLOPE VARIES MATCH FINISHED GRADE OR

AS SHOWN ON PLANS

PARKING LOT CROSS SECTION - MICROMILL

12" CRUSHED STONE OR PROCESSED ——

GRAVEL BEDDING PER RIDOT

COMPACT LEVEL/ STABLE CONC. BASE SEE PLAN FOR -

BINDER COURSE TO REMAIN

A finely shredded, well-aged organic hardwood mulch is the preferred accepted mulch a finely shredded, well-aged organic dark pine mulch may be accepted on a case-bycase basis. Bark dust mulches and wood chips will float and move to the

Ithe bioretention area during a storm event and are not acceptable. Shredded mulch must be well aged (6-12 months) for acceptance. Mix approximately ½ the specified mulch layer into the planting soil to a depth of

approximately 4 inches to help foster a highly organic surface layer. 5.2.4 Compaction

It is very important to minimize compaction of both the base of the bioretention area and the required backfill. When possible, use excavation hoes to remove original soil. If bioretention area is excavated using a loader, the contractor should use wide track or marsh track equipment, or light equipment with turf type tires. Use of equipment with narrow tracks or narrow tires, rubber tires with large lugs, or high pressure tires will cause excessive compaction resulting in reduced infiltration rates and storage volumes and is not acceptable. Compaction will significantly contribute to design failure. Compaction can be alleviated at the base of the bioretention facility by using a primary tilling operation such as a chisel plow, ripper, or subsoiler. These tilling operations are performed to refracture the soil profile through the 12-in compaction zone. Substitute methods must be approved by the engineer. Rototillers typically do not till deep enough

o reduce the effects of compaction from heavy equipment. When backfilling the bioretention facility, place soil in lifts 12in or greater. Do not use heavy equipment within the bioretention basin. Heavy equipment can be used around the perimeter of the basin to supply soils and sand. Grade bioretention materials with light equipment such as a compact loader or a dozer/loader with marsh tracks.

### PROJECT DESCRIPTION

#### Introduction

The Rhode Island Country Club (RICC) located at 150 Nayatt Road in Barrington, RI is proposing the construction of a new multi-use building to accommodate the relocated paddle ball court, new tennis court, replacement of the existing cart barn with a new, larger cart barn. The existing cart barn, storage warehouse, various sheds, and concrete pads will be demolished to accommodate the new facilities. The parking area will also be reconfigured to be more efficient and provide safer circulation. The project area encompasses approximately 2.34 acres and is bound by the recreational facilities to the north, Nayatt Road to the south and Middle Highway to the east. The main building serving RICC is located to the west of the project area.

#### Methodology

Hydrologic calculations for existing and proposed conditions were performed using HydroCAD Version 10.20-5C software, which uses TR-55 methodology to calculate runoff and TR-20 methodology for storm routing through the stormwater detention facilities. Site hydrology was evaluated for the water quality storm (WQ), 1-, 2-, 10-, 25-, and 100-year storms. Existing and Proposed Watershed Maps, indicating the subwatersheds and associated stormwater flow paths can be found in Appendix C.

The project qualifies for redevelopment due to existing conditions consisting of over 40% impervious cover per Title 250 – Department of Environmental Management (DEM) Chapter 150 – Water Resources Subchapter 10 – Wastewater and Stormwater Part 8.12 (B) (2). Further details in the proposed conditions section of this report.

The stormwater drainage design was developed in accordance with March 2015, recodified in 2018 State of Rhode Island Stormwater Design and Installations Standards Manual (RISDISM).

#### Existing Conditions

The watershed area analyzed for the project consists of the Limit of Disturbance (LOD) with a total area of 2.34 acres. The existing site contains approximately 1.37 acres (59%) of impervious area within the LOD, which consists of recreational courts, parking areas, walkways, building roof area, and access drives. The remaining portions of the site are landscaped areas. Stormwater generated on the northern section of the parking lot is directed to drywells located just north of the project area by overland flow. The remainder of the northern portion of the site sheet flows north overland to the golf course. Stormwater on the southern portion of the site flows via overland flow to stormwater structures in Nayatt Road. Overall, the topography slopes to the north, towards the existing golf course from the crest elevation (approximate 23) with remaining area sloping south towards Nayatt Road.

According to the Soil Survey of Rhode Island (US Department of Agriculture Soil Conservation Service 1981), the soils at the project site includes Merrimac fine sandy loam. The on-site soils are classified within Hydrologic Group "A" by the Soil Survey.

Test pits were excavated on October 31st, 2024 to review below grade conditions on the site. The test pit information is provided in Appendix A. The on-site soils are generally comprised of sandy loams and loamy sands in most areas. The estimated seasonal high groundwater table (SHGWT) varies across the site from 36" to 70" below existing grade. The composition of the on-site soils allows for a conservative permeability rate of 2.41 inches/hour in loam sand soils.

Under existing conditions, four sub-watersheds were analyzed, EDA-1, EDA-2, EDA-3, and EDA-4. EDA-1 is comprised of the southern portion of the existing parking lot to the west, access drive to the site, and surrounding landscaped areas. EDA-1 drains to the design point "Nayatt Road". No stormwater structures or other means of conveyance exists in EDA-1. EDA-2 is comprised of the pervious areas south of the access drive to the existing cart barn, storage warehouse and a minor section below the existing paddleball courts which allows stormwater to flow through the court itself to the sloped pervious areas. EDA-2 drains south to the design point "Nayatt Road". EDA-3 is comprised of the northeasterly portion of the site including the existing storage warehouse, cart barn, access drive to the above-mentioned structures, remainder of the paddle-ball court, various sized concrete pads, and landscaped areas throughout. EDA-3 drains to the north to the design point "Golf Course". EDA-4 is comprised of the northly portion of the existing parking lot including landscaped islands. EDA-4 drains to the north to the design point "Golf Course".

#### Proposed Conditions

The proposed development of this site includes the relocation of the existing paddleball courts and demolition of the existing cart barn, storage warehouse, concrete pads, and sheds. The proposed work includes the construction of a new 6,147 square feet (SF) ± cart barn with an extended access drive, a 1,170 SF. ± multi-use building, and tennis court. Site improvements include the construction of walkways, the installation of bioretention areas, other utility improvements, and landscaping. The proposed condition has approximately 1.36 acres of impervious area within the project limits.

The project is going to disturb more than 10,000 SF of the existing impervious area and the existing conditions has 59% existing impervious within the LOD. Due to the amount of existing impervious area within the LOD, the project is considered a redevelopment project. The stormwater system for the project has been designed with the Redevelopment guidelines in the Rhode Island Stormwater Design and Installation Standards Manual. Overall, the project will result in a reduction in impervious area of approximately 333 SF.

The project will include three bioretention areas to treat and mitigate peak runoff rates and volumes. Curb cuts are installed in paved parking areas to convey stormwater runoff to best management practices (BMP's), which are designed to reduce the peak flow rate discharged from the site and provide total suspended solids (TSS) removal. Three bioretention areas have been designed with site grading to convey stormwater to the proper areas.

The existing parking lot is going to be reconfigured to be more efficient. The new impervious areas created in the reconfiguration of the parking lot will be treated to the 1" water quality requirement. Portions of the parking lots are to be micro milled and overlayed which, per redevelopment standards, are not required to be treated. Although not required, due to the existing drainage patterns of the parking lot to be overlayed, the proposed design is treating a section of this area. These areas receiving treatment have been broken down in the Water Quality Requirement Calculations in Appendix B. Approximately 3821 SF of the existing parking lot will be directed to bioretention area (BMP-2) and will be treated for the water quality volume.

The bioretention areas have been designed in accordance with RIDEM Standards to mitigate the peak flow rate and promote the settling of total suspended solids. The bioretention areas include filter media with a mulch layer and 20% by volume of well-aged, well-aerated leaf compost to the planting soil mixture where the SHGWT is 3 feet below grade or less. The inflow to each bioretention area is either directed sheet flow from adjacent areas or channelized runoff via roof runoff conveyance or piped stormwater flow. Sediment forebays are to be installed in each bioretention area for pretreatment of runoff. The outlet of each bioretention area consists of either a riprap slipway, a bleed pipe or both. The bioretention area outlets are raised to store the water quality volume for 24-hours while it slowly drains via infiltration following the storm event. Any runoff that is directed to the bioretention area by piping enters a sediment forebay to receive pretreatment. The golf cart paths throughout the project are a combination of crushed shells and asphalt. To be conservative the CN for all cart paths is modeled as paved.

Under proposed conditions, the site was divided into a total of seven sub-watersheds: PDA-1 through PDA-6.

PDA-1 encompasses the center of the site and includes the proposed cart barn, paddleball court, the tennis court, a portion of the extended accessway to the cart barn, and landscaped areas. The proposed cart barn shall incorporate its runoff flow via downspout collection piping to discharge to the pretreatment area of Bioretention Area No. 1. The tennis court shall drain west to a gravel trench and tie into a trench east of the relocated paddleball court that is directed south to Bioretention Area No. 1. The surrounding pervious area as well as a section of the extended accessway to the cart barn shall be graded and drained via overland flow towards Bioretention Area No. 1. A bleed pipe shall be installed to retain stormwater volume for treatment purposes and will discharge to Bioretention Area No. 2 in PDA-4 via pipe system and ultimately to design point "Golf Course".

A cart washdown area is located off the southwest corner of the cart barn. The cart washdown process is comprised of a power washer hooked up to a hose spigot on the south side of the cart barn. The golf carts are electric, so there is no concern about fuel, oil, or being a LLUPL. No leaners are used during the power washing. The carts will be sprayed down over a crushed stone area that includes a subdrain, which will direct the runoff into the sediment forebay prior to discharging into the bioretention area. The discharge from this bioretention area is directed to a second bioretention system prior to being discharged to the final design point. The bioretention areas have been sized to accommodate this additional volume of runoff. In addition, it is not expected the cart wash area will be utilized during a rain event.

PDA-2 includes the remaining portion of extended cart barn accessway and surrounding landscaped areas. PDA-2 has been graded to direct runoff into Bioretention Area No. 3 by overland flow. The flow directed to the bioretention area will enter into a sediment forebay for pretreatment. Bioretention Area No. 3 is designed to treat the water quality volume, infiltrate the recharge volume, and mitigate peak flows. The larger runoff volumes will be directed over the spillway prior discharging toward the south. This bioretention area will be discharging to the design point "Nayatt Road".

PDA-3 includes the northeast path from the proposed cart barn, existing to remain portions of the cart path, the walkways and landscaped area north of the proposed multi use building, and landscape areas. These areas will retain their existing flow path and will discharge to the design point "Golf Course". The cart path is comprised of combination of crushed shells and impervious area.

PDA-4 includes the proposed multi-use building, adjacent deck structure to the south, walkways adjoining the multi-use building to the parking lot, a portion of existing parking lot, and landscaped areas. PDA-4 has been graded to direct runoff into the sedimentation forebay of Bioretention Area No. 2 by a combination of overland flow, from the parking lot via curb cut, or from the proposed building via downspout collection piping. The runoff from the walkways shall flow overland into the sediment forebay. The runoff piped to the BMP will enter a sediment forebay for pretreatment. Other overland flow directed from the south shall enter the sedimentation forebay located there prior to entry to the bioretention area. Overflow from Bioretention Area 1 will be directed into the sediment forebay prior to discharging north. A bleed pipe has been designed to direct overflow to the north by pipe with flared end with the addition of an overtopping weir acting as a secondary outlet. The bioretention area will be designed to retain the water quality volume and also mitigate the peak flow rate. This bioretention area will discharge to the design point "Golf Course".

PDA-5 includes the southern section of the existing paved parking along with various landscaped areas throughout. This area is only going to be mill and overlayed, therefore does not require stormwater treatment. Due to various site constraints, this area couldn't be captured and directed to a stormwater BMP. This runoff drains south and towards the design point "Nayatt Road".

PDA-6 includes the northern portion of the existing parking area, and landscaped area in the vicinity. This area is only going to be mill and overlayed, therefore does not require stormwater treatment. Due to site constraints, this area couldn't be captured and directed to a BMP. This area drains as it does in existing conditions north into the design point "Golf Course".

The hydrologic model shows a reduction in the peak flow rate and volumes for all design storms at each design point. Tables 1 and 2 below provided a summary of the peak flow rates for the existing and proposed conditions at both design points.

| 25 - Year                  | 22,805               | 13,247   | -9,558  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 100 - Year                 | 37,067               | 25,275   | -11,792 |  |  |  |  |  |  |

#### Water Quality

The proposed stormwater management system has been designed to remove a net annual 90% total suspended solids from the runoff collected from a minimum of 50% of the retaining impervious area and 100% of all new impervious areas per the Redevelopment guidelines in the Rhode Island Stormwater Design and Installation Standards Manual. Several best management practices are proposed to enhance total suspended solids removal. The required WQ to be treated was calculated at 1,522 cubic feet. The proposed design is capable of providing 3,039 cubic feet of WQ volume. The bioretention areas have been designed to detain the water quality volume from upstream areas to allow total suspended solids to settle. See Appendix B for water quality calculations for the stormwater facilities.

#### Minimum Stormwater Management Standards

1. Minimum Standard 1: LID Site Planning and Design Strategies

*"LID Site planning and design strategies must be used to the maximum extent practicable in order to reduce the generation of the water runoff volume for both new and redevelopment projects."* 

LID site planning and design strategies have been employed on this project to the maximum extent practicable.

#### 2. Minimum Standard 2: Groundwater Recharge

*"Stormwater must be recharged within the same sub-watershed to maintain base flow at predevelopment recharge levels to the maximum extent practicable."* 

See Recharge Calculation in Appendix B

Landscape areas and the bioretention areas are allowed to infiltrate and meet the recharge requirements.

#### 3. Minimum Standard 3: Water Quality

*"Stormwater runoff must be treated before discharge."* 

Pre-treatment: Pre-treatment equal to 25% of the water quality volume is required for parking lots, driveways, and sidewalks; no pre-treatment is required for stormwater generated from the building roofs entering infiltration systems. For the parking lot, access drives, and sidewalks pre-treatment is achieved using sedimentation forebays prior to the bioretention areas.

Due to the existing site constraints, it is not feasible to infiltrate or treat the WQV along some portions of the proposed impervious covers. To make up for this deficit, the water quality volumes to the other systems have been increased to ensure the total WQV for the site has been reached, the details of this can be seen in the BMP sizing calculations in Appendix B.

Accordingly, the pre-treatment and treatment requirements of Minimum Standard 3 have been satisfied.

#### 4. Minimum Standard 4: Conveyance and Natural Channel Protection

*"Protection for natural channels downstream must be supplied by providing 24-hour extended detention of the one-year, 24-hour Type III design storm event runoff volume."* 

This standard is waived because the project is a redevelopment site with impervious cover more than 40% of the total site area.

#### 5. Minimum Standard 5: Overbank Flood Protection

*"Downstream overbank flood protection must be provided by attenuating the post-development peak discharge rate to the pre-development levels for the 10-year and 100-year, 24-hour Type III design storm events. In addition, designers must demonstrate that runoff from the Site for storms up to the 100-year, 24-hour Type III design storm events actually reach proposed structural practices designed to meet this criterion."* 

This standard is waived because the project is a redevelopment site with impervious cover more than 40% of the total site area.

#### 6. Minimum Standard 6: Redevelopment and Infill Projects

*"The purpose of this minimum standard is to establish the alternative requirements for projects or portions of a project where existing impervious areas will be redeveloped or where the Site qualifies as infill."* 

This project is considered a redevelopment project due to the existing impervious coverage equating to more than 40% of the total site area.

#### 7. Minimum Standard 7: Pollution Prevention

*"All development Sites require the use of source control and pollution prevention measures to minimize the impact that the land use may have on stormwater runoff quality."* 

Pollution prevention is addressed in the Soil Erosion and Sedimentation Control Plan provided under separate cover, which confirms that Minimum Standard 7 has been satisfied. See the pollutant loading calculations in Appendix B.

#### 8. Minimum Standard 8: Land Uses with Higher Potential Pollutant Loads

*"Stormwater discharges from land uses with higher potential pollutant loads (LUHPPLs) require the use of specific source control and pollution prevention measures and the specific stormwater BMPs approved for such use."* 

In accordance with the *RISDISM* definition, the project is not considered a "land use with higher potential pollutant loads;" therefore Minimum Standard 8 is not applicable to this project.

9. Minimum Standard 9: Illicit Discharges

*"All illicit discharges to stormwater management systems are prohibited."* 

There are no existing or proposed illicit discharges to the stormwater management system; therefore, Minimum Standard 9 is not applicable to this project.

10. Minimum Standard 10: Construction Erosion and Sedimentation Control

*"Erosion and sedimentation control (ESC) practices must be utilized during the construction phase as well as during any land disturbing activities. ESC practices must meet the following minimum design criteria: temporary sediment trapping practices must be sized to store 1 inch of runoff from the contributing area or per the sediment volume method (Rhode Island Soil Erosion and Sediment Control Handbook), whichever is greater; and temporary conveyance practices must be sized to handle the peak flow from the 10-year, 24-hour Type III design storm."* 

NEI developed site plans that include a Proposed Site and Utility Plan, Grading and Drainage Plan, and Detail sheets. These plans have been developed in conformance with the checklist provided in RIPDES CGP Section 5. These plans illustrate the minimum construction erosion and sedimentation controls necessary to meet the requirements of Minimum Standard 10 at the start of construction. Details to control erosion and sediment transport throughout construction are also provided in this plan set.

11. Minimum Standard 11: Stormwater Management Operation and Maintenance

*"The stormwater management system, including all structural stormwater controls and conveyances, must have an operation and maintenance plan to ensure that it continues to function as designed."* 

An Operations and Maintenance Plan has been developed and is provided to the reviewer(s) under separate cover. This document demonstrates compliance with Minimum Standard 11.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, the proposed stormwater management system provides reductions in peak runoff rates and volumes within the hydrologic analysis area for the design storm events evaluated. Additionally, the stormwater management system has been designed to promote total suspended solids removal and to improve the overall water quality to downstream resources and offsite areas. The project reduces the total impervious surfaces compared to the existing conditions.

USDA - NRCS SOIL SURVEY MAP A.P. 6, Lot 1 | 150 Nayatt Road Barrington, Rhode Island

### **LEGEND**

FtA - Fortress sand, 0 to 3 percent slopes

HkC - Hinckley loamy sand, 8 to 15 percent slopes

Mk - Matunuck mucky peat, 0 to 2 percent slopes, very frequently flooded

MmB - Merrimac fine sandy loam, 3 to 8 percent slopes

QoC - Quonset gravelly sandy loam, rolling

Ss - Sudbury sandy loam

SwA - Swansea muck, 0 to 1 percent slopes

Wa - Walpole sandy loam, 0 to 3 percent slopes

#### **Redevelopment Calculations**

Total Area of Site (within LOD) = 102,099 SF Total Existing Impervious Area of Site (within LOD) = 59,810 SF **Existing Impervious Cover % (within LOD)= 59%** >40%

The existing impervious coverage of the site is greater than 40%. This project qualifies as a redevelopment project per 8.12.B.2 of RISDISM

| Total Impervious Area of the Site (LOD)     | 59,477 | SF |                                                                |
|---------------------------------------------|--------|----|----------------------------------------------------------------|
| Proposed Impervious Cover % (within LOD)=   | 58%    |    | 333 SF reduction                                               |
| Total New Impervious =                      | 13,899 | SF | 100% WQV (Landscape to impervious)                             |
| Total Impervious over Existing Impervious = | 18266  | SF | 50% WQV required (new impervious over existing impervious)     |
| Total Resurfaced Impervious Area =          | 25,971 | SF | 0% WQV - (mill & overlay - existing parking area)              |
| Untreated Impervious Area                   | 1,341  | SF | North of the Cart Barn and east of Bio 3 - infeasible to treat |
|                                             |        |    |                                                                |
| Total Impervious Area Treated =             | 54%    |    |                                                                |

#### **Water Quality Calculations**

#### **Bioretention 1**

Total Area of PDA-1= 35,208 SF Total Impervious Area of PDA-1 = 22,100 SF

 Area for New Impervious (1") = 8,051 SF 100% WQV

Impervious Area for Redevelopment (1/2") = 14,048 SF 50% WQV required (redevelopment)

Cell Volume shall be larger of Recharge Volume and Water Quality Volume

**Recharge Volume - Rev**

Total Impervious Area within Hydrologic Group "A" Soils = 22,100 SF F (from RI Stormwater Design & Installation Standards Man. Table 3-4) = 0.60 inches Required Recharge Volume = 1,105 cf

#### **Water Quality Volume (WQV)**

WQV = Total Impervious Area x 1 inch = 671 CF WQV = Total Impervious Area x 1/2 inch = 585 CF

**Required WQV Volume = 1,256 CF Additional Volume from Cart washdown Area = 88 CF Total Required Volume = 1,344 CF**

> Provided Water Quality Volume = **1,994 Total Volume Provided = 1,994 CF** CF @ Elev. 20.30 (Volume below lowest outlet invert from HydroCAD)

#### **Filter Bed Area**

**Af= (WQV)(df)/[(k)(hf+df)(tf)]**

Where : Af = Surface area of filter bed (ft2 )

df = Filter bed depth (ft)

k = Coefficient of permeability of filter media (ft/day) hf = Average height of water above surface of practice

tf = Design filter drain time (days)

 Water Quality Volume (WQV) = 1,256 cf dt = 1.0 ft k= 3.50 ft/day hf = 0.75 ft tf = 0.3 days

**Required Filter Bed Area Af = 684 SF Provided Surface Area = 1,184 SF Area of System from HydroCAD**

#### **Pretreatment Volume**

#### **Water Quality Volume (WQV)**

WQV = Impervious Area treated by Sediment Forebay x 1 inches = 1,256 CF Required Pretreatment Volume = 25% WQV = 314 CF **Pretreatment Volume Provided = 659 CF** Sediment forebay in bioretention area (Includes Cart Barn Roof) Store 25% of water quality volume

#### **Drawdown within 48 hours**

Time = (Provided Volume) / (K x Bottom Area)

Provided Volume = **1,994 CF**

**FT/DAY (from Section 5.5.4 of the RI Stormwater & Installation Standards Manual)**

Required Bottom Area (Average) = **1,184 SF**

K = saturated hydraulic conductivity = **1.02**

Time (hrs) = **40 hrs < 48 hrs**

#### **Cart Washdown Calculations**

Heavy Duty Power Washer produces 3 gallons per minute

| Time per Cart times (75 Carts)                                     | 3       | Min                    |  |
|--------------------------------------------------------------------|---------|------------------------|--|
| Number of Carts<br>Power Washer                                    | 75<br>3 | Unit<br>Gallons/minute |  |
| Volume ( 1 Gallon = 0.13 CF)                                       | 88      | CF                     |  |
| Crushed Stone within cart wash area (5' wide x 42' long x 1' deep) | 210     | CF                     |  |
| Volume provided in crushed stone (33% Voids) =                     | 69      | CF                     |  |

The 88 CF of runoff is assuming all 75 carts are washed at the same time, therefore between the Bioretention Area being oversized and the storage volume within the cart washing area the volume provided is more than adequate to treat and mitigate the runoff.

### STORMWATER O&M Plan

![](RICC Full Preliminary Package 3-4-25_attachments/_page_134_Picture_1.jpeg)

## Proposed Development Project RICC "Southeast Corner"

## Nayatt Road Barrington, RI 02806

Assessors Plat 06, Lot 001 Zoned Recreational and Education Issued 2-10-25

#### Property Owner:

Dan Cregan 150 Nayatt Road Barrington, RI 02806

#### Applicant/Operator:

Dan Cregan 150 Nayatt Road Barrington, RI 02806 T: 401.245.5700 x102 E: dan.cregan@cbre.com

Prepared by Joe Malo, PE

NEI Job Number: 23.0187

Prepared by: Narragansett Engineering, Inc. 3102 East Main St, Portsmouth, RI 02871

#### EXISTING SITE CONDITIONS

Under existing conditions, the Area of Concern (AOC) includes a number of stormwater best management practices (BMPs) to control stormwater quality and quantity for the development. BMPs proposed for the project include multiple bioretention facilities. The AOC includes a proposed a multi-use building, cart barn with cart path, tennis court, relocated paddleball court, parking, and drive isles.

#### Short-term Requirements

Once construction has been completed, more frequent inspections and required maintenance shall be performed during the first growing season. These inspections shall be performed weekly during the first month after construction is completed and monthly for the remainder of the first growing season. The goal of these inspections is to ensure that no erosion of the partially stabilized soils is occurring. Any erosion that is observed shall be remedied quickly by repairing and reseeding as necessary

#### OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE PLAN

The stormwater management system, including all structural stormwater controls and conveyances, must have an operation and management plan to ensure that it continues to function as designed. The plan shall identify measures for implementing maintenance activities in a manner that minimizes stormwater runoff impacts. The owners of the lot will be responsible for the operation and maintenance of the site, the estimated budget, and the funding for the activities and equipment required. A legally binding and enforceable maintenance agreement shall be executed between the facility owner and the responsible authority to ensure the following:

#### REQUIRED ELEMENTS

#### Bioretention Maintenance:

The bioretention area shall be inspected annually and after every major storm of 1 inch or greater for trash, debris, sediment, erosion, standing water, and overall performance. Defects shall be repaired by the owner.

The owner shall mow grass within bioretention area twice annually, once in late spring and once in early fall. The vegetation shall not exceed 18" in height. The owner shall re-mulch bioretention area in spring every year. In spring, the owner shall trim vegetation and remove dead vegetation from bioretention area.

Remove accumulated sediment from the bioretention cells annually in the spring or if sediment exceeds 1" in the bioretention area cells.

If standing water is observed more than 48 hours after a storm event, then the top 6 inches of material shall be removed and replaced with new materials in kind. If discolored or contaminated material is found below this removed surface then that material shall also be removed and replaced until all contaminated material has been removed from the filter chamber. The material shall be disposed of in accordance with all applicable federal and local regulations.

Narragansett Engineering, Inc. February 10, 2025 Job Number – 23.0187

#### Sediment Forebay Maintenance:

Inspections shall be performed quarterly of the sediment forebay or following storm events with rainfall exceeding 1". Inspect for sediment, overall performance and erosion. Sediment shall be removed when it is exceeding half the design depth. Trash and debris shall be removed in the spring and the fall.

The grass shall be mowed on the side slopes and embankments a minimum 3 times between May and September. The basin setback and embankment shall be mowed annually and the basin shall be mowed every other year.

#### Catch Basin Maintenance:

The catch basins will also need inspection and cleaning as sediment reaches a depth of 1 foot.

#### Bleed Pipe:

The bleed pipes shall be inspected annually and after storm events greater than 1". Inspect for overall performance, trash, debris and erosion.

#### Riprap Spillway:

The riprap spillways shall be inspected annually and after storm events greater than 1". Inspect for overall performance, trash, debris and erosion.

#### Long-Term Maintenance of Non-Stormwater Related Activities

Solid Waste Containment: Solid waste shall be collected by a licensed waste disposal firm on a regular basis and disposed of off-site in conformance with all applicable regulatory standards.

Snow Disposal: Snow shall be removed from all drives, parking areas, fire access drive, and sidewalks whenever an accumulation of snow occurs by the owner/operator or a private licensed subcontractor. No snow shall be plowed in or adjacent to catch basins or stormwater areas.

Lawn and Landscape Management: The Owner shall employ the standards for ground management specified in Appendix G (G.7) of the RISDISM to the extent practicable. This includes mowing to a height of no less than two inches during the growing season, and minimization of fertilizers, pesticides, and irrigation. All landscaping and landscaping maintenance shall be performed by a licensed subcontractor or property owner and all materials removed from the premises shall be in conformance with all applicable regulatory standards.

#### Stormwater Facility Maintenance Agreement

| THIS AGREEMENT, made and entered into this                                                                                                            |                                    | day<br>of | , 20 , by                                  |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------|-----------|--------------------------------------------|
| and<br>between                                                                                                                                        |                                    |           | hereinafter                                |
| called the "Landowner", and the Town of Barrington                                                                                                    |                                    |           | , hereinafter called the "Town".           |
| WITNESSETH, that WHEREAS, the Landowner is the owner of certain real property                                                                         |                                    |           |                                            |
| described<br>as                                                                                                                                       |                                    |           | , as recorded by deed in the               |
| land<br>records<br>of                                                                                                                                 | _, Deed                            | Book      | ,                                          |
| Page                                                                                                                                                  | hereinafter called the "Property". |           |                                            |
| WHEREAS, the Landowner is proceeding to build on and develop the property; and                                                                        |                                    |           |                                            |
| WHEREAS, the Site Plan/Subdivision Plan known                                                                                                         | as                                 |           |                                            |
|                                                                                                                                                       |                                    |           | _, hereinafter called the "Plan", which is |
| expressly made a part hereof, as approved or to be approved by the Town, provides<br>for detention of stormwater within the confines of the property; |                                    | and       |                                            |
|                                                                                                                                                       |                                    |           |                                            |

WHEREAS, the Town and the Landowner, its successors and assigns, agree that the health, safety, and welfare of the residents of the Town require that on-site stormwater management facilities be constructed and maintained on the Property; and

WHEREAS, the Town requires that on-site stormwater management facilities as shown on the Plan be constructed and adequately maintained by the Landowner, its successors and assigns.

NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of the foregoing premises, the mutual covenants contained herein, and the following terms and conditions, the parties hereto agree as follows:

- 1. The on-site stormwater management facilities shall be constructed by the Landowner, its successors and assigns, in accordance with the plans and specifications identified in the Plan.
- 2. The Landowner, its successors and assigns, shall adequately maintain the stormwater management facilities in accordance with the required Operation and Maintenance Plan. This includes all pipes, channels or other conveyances built to convey stormwater to the facility, as well as all structures, improvements, and vegetation provided to control the quantity and quality of the stormwater. Adequate maintenance is herein defined as good working condition so that these facilities are performing their design functions. The Stormwater Best Management Practices Operation, Maintenance and Management Checklists are to be used to establish what good working condition is acceptable to the Town.

- 3. The Landowner, its successors and assigns, shall inspect the stormwater management facility as required in the Operation and Maintenance Plan. The purpose of the inspection is to assure safe and proper functioning of the facilities. The inspection shall cover the entire facilities, berms, outlet structures, basin areas, access roads, etc. Deficiencies shall be noted in an inspection report.
- 4. The Landowner, its successors and assigns, hereby grant permission to the Town, its authorized agents and employees, to enter upon the Property and to inspect the stormwater management facilities whenever the Town deems necessary upon 48-hours's notice by the Town. The purpose of inspection is to follow-up on reported deficiencies and/or to respond to citizen complaints. The Town shall provide the Landowner, its successors and assigns, copies of the inspection findings and a directive to commence with the repairs if necessary.
- 5. In the event the Landowner, its successors and assigns, fails to maintain the stormwater management facilities in good working condition acceptable to the Town, upon 72 hours' notice the Town may enter upon the Property and take whatever steps necessary to correct deficiencies identified in the inspection report and to charge the costs of such repairs to the Landowner, its successors and assigns. This provision shall not be construed to allow the Town to erect any structure of permanent nature on the land of the Landowner outside of the easement for the stormwater management facilities. It is expressly understood and agreed that the Town is under no obligation to routinely maintain or repair said facilities, and in no event shall this Agreement be construed to impose any such obligation on the Town.
- 6. The Landowner, its successors and assigns, will perform the work necessary to keep these facilities in good working order as appropriate. In the event a maintenance schedule for the stormwater management facilities (including sediment removal) is outlined on the approved plans, the schedule will be followed.
- 7. In the event the Town pursuant to this Agreement, performs work of any nature, or expends any funds in performance of said work for labor, use of equipment, supplies, materials, and the like, the Landowner, its successors and assigns, shall reimburse the Town upon demand, within thirty (30) days of receipt thereof for all actual costs incurred by the Town hereunder.
- 8. This Agreement imposes no liability of any kind whatsoever on the Town and the Landowner agrees to hold the Town harmless from any liability in the event the stormwater management facilities fail to operate properly.
- 9. This Agreement shall be recorded among the land records of the Town and shall constitute a covenant running with the land, and shall be binding on the Landowner, its administrators, executors, assigns, heirs and any other successors in interests.

Narragansett Engineering, Inc. ### **GENERAL NOTES & SPECIFICATIONS:**

1. ALL WORK SHALL CONFORM TO ALL APPLICABLE LOCAL STATE AND FEDERAL CODES.
2. ALL MATERIALS, FIXTURES, EQUIPMENT & APPLIANCES SHALL BE INSTALLED IN ACCORDANCE WITH MANUFACTURE'S INSTRUCTIONS & LOCAL BUILDING CODES.
3. ALL WORK SHALL BE REPEORMED BY MECHANICS SKILLED IN THEIR PESPECTIVE TRADES.

3. ALL WORK SHALL BE PERFORMED BY MECHANICS SKILLED IN THEIR RESPECTIVE TRADES.
4. ALL CONTRACTORS ARE RESPONSIBLE FOR CUTTING, PATCHING, FILLING, AND CLEANING UP AFTER THEIR OWN WORK.

5. ALL CONTRACTORS SHALL HOLD INTENT OF THE DRAWINGS WHICH IS TO PROVIDE COMPLETE AND FINISH WORK, TESTED AND GUARANTEED FOR A MINIMUM OF 1 YEAR FROM THE TIME OF COMPLETION.

6. IN NO EVENT SHALL STRUCTURAL MEMBERS BE CUT OR DRILLED WITHOUT THE WRITTEN APPROVAL OF THE DESIGNER.

7. ALL CHANGES SHALL BE REQUESTED ON WRITING AND APPROVED IN WRITING BY THE DESIGNER.
8. ALL WASTE AND REMOVALS SHALL BE DISPOSED OF LEGALLY OFF SITE.
9. UPON COMPLETION OF THE CONTRACT, EACH CONTRACTOR SHALL CLEAN UP AFTER HIS WORK, REMOVING ALL DEBRIS INSIDE AND OUTSIDE THE BUILDING CREATED BY HIS WORK. EACH

SUBJECT TO THE APPROVAL OF THE OWNER.

10. THE DESIGNER HAS THE RIGHT TO REJECT ANY SLOPPY, POORLY INSTALLED, OR UNAUTHORIZED WORK OR WORK DONE CONTRARY TO THE INTENT OF THE CONTRACT DOCUMENTS. SUCH WORK

SHALL BE REPLACED, REPAIRED AND REMOVED AT CONTRACTORS EXPENSE.

11. THE CONTRACTOR IS RESPONSIBLE FOR ALL MEANS AND METHODS OF TEMPORARY SHORING

12. THE CONTRACTOR AND ALL SUB-CONTRACTORS SHALL VERIFY ALL DIMENSIONS AND CONDITIONS AT THE SITE, AND SHALL NOTIFY THE DESIGNER OF ANY DISCREPANCY. CROSS-CHECK DETAILS AND DIMENSIONS SHOWN ON DRAWINGS.

13. IN ALL CASES WHERE A CONFLICT MAY OCCUR SUCH AS BETWEEN ITEMS COVERED BY SPECIFICATIONS AND NOTES ON THE DRAWINGS, OR BETWEEN GENERAL NOTES AND SPECIFIC DETAILS, THE DESIGNER SHALL BE NOTIFIED AND WILL INTERPRET THE INTENT OF THE CONTRACT DOCUMENTS.

14. FLOOR AND WALL OPENINGS, SLEEVES, VARIATION IN THE STRUCTURAL SLAB ELEVATIONS, DEPRESSED AREAS AND ALL OTHER ARCHITECTURAL, MECHANICAL, ELECTRICAL AND CIVIL REQUIREMENTS MUST BE COORDINATED BEFORE THE CONTRACTOR PROCEEDS WITH CONSTRUCTION.

15. WORKMANSHIP AND MATERIALS SHALL CONFORM TO THE REQUIREMENTS OF THE BUILDING CODES ACTIVE AT THE TIME OF THE PERMIT.

16. FOR RENOVATION WORK, DRAWINGS ARE PRODUCED WITH ASSUMPTIONS MADE REGARDING

EXISTING CONDITIONS. IF CONTRACTOR FINDS EXISTING CONDITIONS NOT AS ASSUMED CONTACT ARCHITECT IMMEDIATELY.

17. NELL CARPENTRY WORK SHALL BE EXECUTED IN CONFORMANCE WITH THE RHODE ISLAND STATE

BUILDING CODE.

18. DO NOT SCALE DRAWINGS. ALL DIMENSIONS FOR INTERIOR WALLS ARE TO FINISH FACE OF WALL UNLESS OTHERWISE NOTE.

### **STRUCTURAL NARRATIVE:**

### Foundation

Poured in place reinforced concrete footings that are approximately 12inches thick and 24 inches wide

Poured in place reinforced concrete foundation walls that are either 8 or 10 inches thick depending on their height

Intermediate poured in place concrete spread footings as required to support any load bearing columns

The foundation will have cast in place anchor bolts at the necessary spacing to effectively anchor the framing to

1st Floor Framing
A center beam line most likely framed with laminated veneer lumber (LVL) that is supported by concrete filled lally columns

Engineered I-Joist recommended for the floors. Most likely 9 1/2 inch depth will be adequate. Traditional

dimensional lumber may be an option if so chosen

Floor sheathing will be 3/4 inch thick tongue and groove structural sheathing

The roof will be sheathed with 5/8" tongue and groove structural sheathing

Walls
Walls will be framed with 2x6 stude at 16 inches on cent

Walls will be framed with 2x6 studs at 16 inches on center
Walls will be sheathed with 1/2 inch thick structural sheathing
A structural shearwall package for the lateral stability of the structure will be required which includes designar shearwalls and holdown locations

Roof
The vaulted space will be framed with pre-engineered scissor trusses at 24 inches on center
The flat ceiling spaces will be framed with traditional flat bottom chord pre-engineered trusses at 24 inches

13. IN ALL CASES WHERE A CONFLICT MAY OCCUR SUCH AS BETWEEN ITEMS COVERED BY SPECIFICATIONS AND NOTES ON THE DRAWINGS, OR BETWEEN GENERAL NOTES AND SPECIFIC DETAILS, THE DESIGNER SHALL BE NOTIFIED AND WILL INTERPRET THE INTENT OF THE CONTRACT

14. FLOOR AND WALL OPENINGS, SLEEVES, VARIATION IN THE STRUCTURAL SLAB ELEVATIONS, DEPRESSED AREAS AND ALL OTHER ARCHITECTURAL, MECHANICAL, ELECTRICAL AND CIVIL REQUIREMENTS MUST BE COORDINATED BEFORE THE CONTRACTOR PROCEEDS WITH

15. WORKMANSHIP AND MATERIALS SHALL CONFORM TO THE REQUIREMENTS OF THE BUILDING CODES ACTIVE AT THE TIME OF THE PERMIT.

16. FOR RENOVATION WORK, DRAWINGS ARE PRODUCED WITH ASSUMPTIONS MADE REGARDING EXISTING CONDITIONS. IF CONTRACTOR FINDS EXISTING CONDITIONS NOT AS ASSUMED CONTACT ARCHITECT IMMEDIATELY.

17. ALL CARPENTRY WORK SHALL BE EXECUTED IN CONFORMANCE WITH THE RHODE ISLAND STATE BUILDING CODE.

18. DO NOT SCALE DRAWINGS. ALL DIMENSIONS FOR INTERIOR WALLS ARE TO FINISH FACE OF WALL UNLESS OTHERWISE NOTE.

### STRUCTURAL NARRATIVE:

Poured in place reinforced concrete footings that are approximately 12inches thick and 24 inches wide Poured in place reinforced concrete foundation walls that are either 8 or 10 inches thick depending on their height

Intermediate poured in place concrete spread footings as required to support any load bearing columns The foundation will have cast in place anchor bolts at the necessary spacing to effectively anchor the framing to the foundation

1st Floor Framing A center beam line most likely framed with laminated veneer lumber (LVL) that is supported by concrete filled lally Engineered I-Joist recommended for the floors. Most likely 9 1/2 inch depth will be adequate. Traditional

dimensional lumber may be an option if so chosen Floor sheathing will be 3/4 inch thick tongue and groove structural sheathing

Walls will be framed with 2x6 studs at 16 inches on center

Walls will be sheathed with 1/2 inch thick structural sheathing

A structural shearwall package for the lateral stability of the structure will be required which includes designated shearwalls and holdown locations

The vaulted space will be framed with pre-engineered scissor trusses at 24 inches on center The flat ceiling spaces will be framed with traditional flat bottom chord pre-engineered trusses at 24 inches on The roof will be sheathed with 5/8" tongue and groove structural sheathing

#### **Re: Landscape Island Tree Sustainability** – **Rhode Island County Club (RICC) (23.0187)**

After careful consideration, we have reviewed the use of the permavoid ( [Permavoid -](https://www.permavoid.com/) Sustainable [Water Management Solutions](https://www.permavoid.com/) ) (or similar system) for the landscape island in the parking area at the Rhode Island Country Club (RICC). While permavoid is a valuable system for urban environments, we have determined that it is not necessary for this specific location based on current conditions. It is also noted that is stormwater is being captured and treated on site in the form of bio-retention areas.

The new landscape island within the parking area is at its narrowest 4 feet within the curbs. The island is continuous with an overall area of 1,200 square feet and will provide an adequate soil volume to support the proposed London Plane trees and perennials and ornamental grasses. All plant material is durable and was selected based on ability to withstand conditions like this. All plant beds within the site will be prepared in accordance with the planting details and specifications noted on LP1.22.

If you have any questions do not hesitate to reach out to the Traverse office or email [aiannuccilli@traversela.com.](mailto:aiannuccilli@traversela.com)
